< Review>
One of my favorite parks in PV neighborhood. The park is supposed clean and extremely well maintained. The park overlooks the scenic drive from Hawthorne going into Palos Verdes and is a great place to get a birds eye view of the Pacific ocean. The kids play area is fantastic and you can rent toys from the park administration office. Fond memories of visiting this park so many times in the last few years.There is also a basketball court for folks to play.</Review>

< review>
Nice, clean, quiet & safe place to enjoy your kids.  There are nice BBQ grills and pits too.
Caution: when the park staff(it's PV, of course there's staff) tells you the gates are gonna lock at 6:30, they do not mean 6:30.plus 15 seconds. Those gates lock. Everything not outside the gates starts inside until morning.</review>

<user_id>106139593724702083601</user_id><user_name>Dan Urban<//user_name><Time>1555904117793<//Time><Rate>5<//Rate>< text>
This is a great local park! The whole park is set into the hills in Palos Verdes overing the ocean, so there are some great views. There are fields, tennis courts, basketball courts, and play apparatus. I really like that the pay apparatus are themed to look like pirate ships. You can borrow sports equipment from the staff, and there are available bathrooms and water fountains. There are also picnic areas with grills for cooking. On a nice day, this is a hard park to beat. Just bring a jacket because the breeze off the ocean can be chilly.<//text>

Bianca Napoles</username>
< date>
1534533505177</date>
<Rate>5< /Rate>< Review>
Lovely park.
A playground with 2 stations, lots of picnic tables, some grills, massive amount of grass and greenery, a good amount of trees if you're looking for shaded areas, and a large section in the back- off to the right- if you're looking for privacy.
If you'll be in that area, please keep the noise level down.  There is a golf course on one side and backyards/homes on the other. ;)
One issue (that can't be helped), the whole park is on a downward sloping hill, so you park and enter at the top, then you have to walk down a good amount of steps (or a ramp) just to get to the bathrooms/office/basketball courts, then more steps to get to the playground.  If you want to go further into the grassy area, more downwards.
This can be tough if you decided to picnic and are now bringing everything back up.  Even worse if your toddler took you down there to explore and now refuses to walk back!!</Review>

<rate>2< /rate>< Text>
We have used Ernie's for three moves in the past few years. I have never felt overcharged until now.  The estimate they gave me was 130.00 (1 hour basically) under what they billed me.  Beware of the " Double Drive Time" policy - I was told that all movers do this.  The explanation was "Double Talk" for you are paying double for your actual move.  That is the time the truck is on the road from where your stuff is loaded to where it is unloaded.  Basically, it helps pay for the time it takes to drive to the loading point from their facility and then back to their facility from the unloading point.  They tell you that you don't pay for it but, you do.  I was also told that the policy doesn't always work in their favor - the example used was that if they did a move in Sac. and the client was only moving a couple of miles away, they would basically lose money because they would drive all the way to Sac for free, then double the drive time for just those couple of miles between the old and new homes and then drive all the way back to Grass Valley from Sac. for free.  My move was the opposite.  They drove to Auburn for free, loaded an item and drove to Penn Valley (1 hour - Doubled! to 2) dropped off the item and drove from PV to GV for free.  I paid almost 400.00 for that!  The estimate was 2 hours at 128.00 .  I called to object to the excessive charge and was told "that's business" and was given a 34.00 credit because the loading did take longer than it should have.
I guess I helped pay for one of those moves when the doubling thing doesn't work in their favor.</Text>

<date>1548451650846< /date><rating>5<//rating><Review>On a Thursday at noon, I passed by The Everest Momo, and I had to stop. I grew up eating chow mein in Calcutta, India and momos in Jackson Heights, New York. I wanted to see if this food would take me back.

The lunch rush was just beginning. There were six people ahead of me. I was in line for less than five minutes.

< review>
It was a very good experience eating here with my kids. They are very picky eaters but loved the chicken momo. The veggie momo and veggie fried rice was extremely tastey. You get a good portion for the price and it was very inexpensive for that area. The menu was very limited but it worked because the food came out very fast. The service was phenomenal. My kids asked if we can return soon. The only suggestion I have is for them to keep their door close during business hours. After we left the restaurant last night, we saw at least 6-7 rats running around in the plaza area near the street. <time>1555045865058</time><Rate>3</Rate><Review>I don't normally make the effort to give three stars, but this place deserves since feedback. I had the veggie Momo's and noodles combo for lunch. I'm a huge eater , finished everything and was way too full for the next 10 hours. This is stick to your bones kind of food and giant athlete size portions.

The sauces were a bit odd - specifically the Momo sauce, that I would skip next time.

The real dent to stars Congress to the presentation. Everything was served to go, regardless of dining in our not. This is went and misleading in several fronts. First off , Oakland has that dumb dine in tax. So if you say "for here" you pay the dumb tax. Either way you get a compostable container filled with foil and possibly (not really) compostable forks. These are dumplings, they don't need that sort of overpackaging. Moreover, because the foil and paper are mixed, their own waste streams were a mess.

Take note, don't serve everything like this. It's a cop out. Serve some real plates and utensils for dining in and do some dishes. I don't want to have a giant pile of trash in front of me after I eat. That model is broken and unsustainable, literally and figuratively.< /Review><pics>None<//pics>< Resp>

<Resp>None<//Resp>< text>
Best burrito joint in SF and I have been to all of the biggies. Not the most stylish place but they always come through.  Burritos are much better than tacos here.< /text>
<gmap_id>0x808f7e1e0476e14f:0x900216b5547e3f89</gmap_id><user>109902966496053707958< /user><pics>None< /pics></record>
</dataset><record>
<Rating>5<//Rating><user_name>rudi rughoonundon<//user_name>< review>
We eat at el castillito once a week and i have been eating there for almost 2 decades now.

I consider it to be one of the top 3 taquerias in san francisco.

In my opinion they have the best al pastor (marinated pork) in the entire city.

The super meat burrito is substantial enough that we often split one between 2 people.

The super tacos are the perfect lunch/afternoon snack.

We live around the corner but i often go there to sit at the window and people watch while having tacos.

Some people may also like how they ask you the type of beans, rice and other fillings right there as they are making it in front of you.

My recommendation (careful as this is mucho caliente): regular meat burrito with al pastor, black beans, spicy salsa, everything on it, extra jalalenos, extra salsa roja.

The chips are not the best in the city but they are good enough. The salsa bar has the basics.</review>

Probably one of the better taquerias in this area of town. The beef and the chicken are fantastic. I want the pork to be good given the tasty spit they have hanging but unfortunately it is dry :(. Burritos are huge, their  tacos are also of large size for a relatively reasonable price. All and all this place is a great place to get the Mission fix outside of the Mission.</Text>

Bernard K< /username>
<date>1534923819204<//date><Rating>5< /Rating><Text>This is the type of Mexican restaurant that will make every New Yorker stop dead in their tracks. Unassuming. Rugged. Authentic. It's the type of cuisine you'd expect to only find in the depths of Parts Unknown, but allas here we are in the center of it all, San Francisco.

This isn't your grandma's ricearoni joint. This is straight up south of the border home cooking. Every man has his vice. At El Castillito, expertly named for a famous castle, I found mine...the vegetarian burrito.

Ordering from the man behind the counter repping the SF Giants hat, I can tell he is ready for business...he is ready to serve up the burrito that will make my night. Assertive, yet attentive, he asks me to make some of the hardest choices of the evening. Black beans or pinto beans? Cilantro? You get the drill. Once the bad boy is all wrapped up, he gives it another 30 seconds on the oven to heat up to a perfected crisp. Perfection at last.

After paying what is due, I make sure to grab some salsas and slather my burrito up. It's time to induldge. The crescendo of the evening is finally here. I take the first bite, the salsa verde hitting my palate doesn't hold back. Excellence. They don't make it this good in NYC. The first bite, game over. This is it. Satisfaction at long last. And I still have the entire burrito to go.

If you're in the neighborhood, try El Castillito. You won't be disappointed. And if you are, it's definitely you.</Text><Pics>None<//Pics><resp>None<//resp><gmap_id>0x808f7e1e0476e14f:0x900216b5547e3f89</gmap_id></record>

< Text>
Probably one of the better taquerias in this area of town. The beef and the chicken are fantastic. I want the pork to be good given the tasty spit they have hanging but unfortunately it is dry :(. Burritos are huge, their  tacos are also of large size for a relatively reasonable price. The torta is an interesting little bit worth getting but probably also worth splitting with someone since it is huge. All and all this place is a great place to get the Mission fix outside of the Mission.</Text>

I have been eating here for over ten years, and I have yet to find a burrito anywhere in the City I actually prefer over a good Chorizo Super Burrito on a Spinach tortilla with salsa verde and fresh juice from El Castillito. Rather conveniently, it isn‚Äôt too far from where I live either. Even if it feels like too much food that day, they have excellent tacos and tortas, just perfect for when you want something light, but zesty!

If you ever find yourself on this part of Church St., do stop by and check it out, I guarantee you will not regret it!</Text>

<user_id>112235208551022567251</user_id>< Name>
Eve Hu< /Name>
<time>1414449078953< /time><Rate>5</Rate>< text>
Get the green tomatillo sauce. I don't care if you're only there for a glass of freshly made (squeezed? pressed?) carrot juice: get the green tomatillo sauce. It is just creamy and just spicy enough to be the perfect complement to any item on the menu at El Castillito.

The quesadilla el castillito (con pollo o carne asada) is a perennial favorite and a worthy vessel for the green tomatillo salsa. The friendly cook always tricks me into speaking Spanish, and I oblige up until he asks me what kind of beans I want with my quesadilla and I have to say, "Frijoles...uh...refried-o".

Another secret is the vegetable burrito, which you can pair with the green tomatillo sauce. The vegetable burrito is packed with grilled veggies and is both cheaper and tastier than the plain bean and rice business that is the vegetarian burrito.

You can ask for chips at the cash register. I always do because eating chips dipped in green tomatillo salsa is normal and drinking a cup of green tomatillo salsa neat is not.< /text>
